  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_85955455-82ac-448e-be33-7940510fe8fe'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText2817498487272282549" style="display:none"><i>Jack appeared at my door last night after six months of no communication wearing a Mets jersey and holding a dozen red roses. He told me he was sorry, that he loved me, and that he would earn my trust again. It took everything in me to not fall apart at the mere sight of him. I wanted to take him back into my life, but I needed to know that this time it would be forever…</i><br /><br />In J. Sterling’s highly anticipated follow-up to her USA Today bestselling novel The Perfect Game, Jack and Cassie quickly realize that their new lifestyle can often be cruel and unforgiving. Their happiness is put to the test as the past is never truly far behind. <br /><br />How do you stay together when the world's trying to tear you apart?</span>

          </div>
    </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer482572973" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2425314971771344639"><b><u>2.5 Stars!</u><br/><br/>Dragged up, over the top dramatic and not needed are the few words that come to my mind when I think how I'd label this book.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/611112.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Even if the people begged, and the author wrote a continuation at least it should have been something interesting and mental like the first book. NO. It was forced upon randomly.<br/>The first book nicely ends in a simple epilogue.. if needed the author c</span>
  <span id="freeText2425314971771344639" style="display:none"><b><u>2.5 Stars!</u><br><br>Dragged up, over the top dramatic and not needed are the few words that come to my mind when I think how I'd label this book.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/611112.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even if the people begged, and the author wrote a continuation at least it should have been something interesting and mental like the first book. NO. This was so cliché, the kind that "I've been there and read that types."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401601ra/779734.gif" width="330" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>According to me, this book was NOT NEEDED. It was forced upon randomly.<br>The first book nicely ends in a simple epilogue.. if needed the author could have given us a novella about their lives after their HEA in book one but NO;<br><br>This book picks up after the last chapter of book1 and not the epilogue. The pace starts of slow but then nicely picks up but then the drama begins but it was so stupid and over the top.<br><br>THE FIRST BOOK WAS 50 TIMES BETTER THAN THIS. I AM DISAPPOINTED EVEN THOUGH I DIDN'T KEEP MY EXPECTATIONS HIGH.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396193ra/763467.gif" width="320" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Maybe others will like it, but for me it was very meh.. I liked where book 1 ended. It was just more better in the terms of ending.. maybe if this book had started after the epilogue of book1 would I might have liked it more.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer147251619358400688">Am I the only one who is hoping that this sequel isnt real, or that if its real, its actually just The Perfect Game told from the perspective of another character? The way The Perfect Game ended was fine. Cassie and Jack's story seemed over to me. The only reason I could think of as to why there would be a sequel is that Jack is gonna fuck up. Again. And in all honesty, I'm not interested in having my heart ripped out by him again. The first book ended with the two of them living "happily ever a</span>
  <span id="freeText147251619358400688" style="display:none">Am I the only one who is hoping that this sequel isnt real, or that if its real, its actually just The Perfect Game told from the perspective of another character? The way The Perfect Game ended was fine. Cassie and Jack's story seemed over to me. The only reason I could think of as to why there would be a sequel is that Jack is gonna fuck up. Again. And in all honesty, I'm not interested in having my heart ripped out by him again. The first book ended with the two of them living "happily ever after" (I wasnt too happy about it though. Jack should have suffered more before Cassie even considered being with him again in my opinion), so why ruin that with a sequel? But that's just my two cents. As of right now, I don't want to read this, because I'm scared of what else could possibly go wrong, but I may change my mind later.</span>

<div id="review_474078077" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474078077" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474078077?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474078077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7402853859498917257"><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/d406467a-d810-4258-8faa-576b7d34d710_zpsa0dc7c4a.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400340i/775612._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo d406467a-d810-4258-8faa-576b7d34d710_zpsa0dc7c4a.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>So... looking at the reviews for this one, it seems like readers will either LOVE it or HATE it... not much in-between... I for one LOVED IT! <br/>Jack Carter is my ALL TIME favorite Jerk. Is it just me, or do you all just melt when he calls Cassie ‘Kitten’? Even though Jack was far from perfect in The Perfect Game, I still fell for him. For all those that didn’t love Jack in book one, he really turns it around in this one, and for all those like me who loved him in book one, you will love him mo</span>
  <span id="freeText7402853859498917257" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/d406467a-d810-4258-8faa-576b7d34d710_zpsa0dc7c4a.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400340i/775612._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo d406467a-d810-4258-8faa-576b7d34d710_zpsa0dc7c4a.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So... looking at the reviews for this one, it seems like readers will either LOVE it or HATE it... not much in-between... I for one LOVED IT! <br>Jack Carter is my ALL TIME favorite Jerk. Is it just me, or do you all just melt when he calls Cassie ‘Kitten’? Even though Jack was far from perfect in The Perfect Game, I still fell for him. For all those that didn’t love Jack in book one, he really turns it around in this one, and for all those like me who loved him in book one, you will love him more in this one! <br><br><br>The Perfect Game... a book that I loved, but gave me mass anxiety. Jack Carter. Oh Jack. Jack screwed up royally in The Perfect Game. But he is a changed man. He is ready to do what ever it takes to get things right between him and the love of his life. He has spent the last six months trying to get himself together, right all his wrongs. He isn’t a whole man without Cassie. He needs her, and only her. <br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“It’s either Cassie for me or no one.”</i>
  </blockquote>
</b> The Game Changer starts where The Perfect Game left off... Jack got himself traded to the NY Mets so he could be closer to Cassie and try to win her back. It has been six months since the two have talked or spent anytime together. Both are still very much in love with one another, but Jack made a huge mistake. A mistake that almost ruined everything. Cassie has forgiven him. But trying to forget and moving on from the past is another story.<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/15b9a6b2-acf2-4133-90ca-d3221c5da43b_zps99942211.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400340i/775613.jpg" alt=" photo 15b9a6b2-acf2-4133-90ca-d3221c5da43b_zps99942211.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I loved the first bit of the book- we got to see Jack reflect on the past. He told Cassie all about what has been going on the last six months, explaining to her why it took so long for him to contact her. He wanted to do the right thing for once. <br><b>
  <blockquote>“I know I don’t deserve you, but I need you.”</blockquote>
</b><br>All Jack wants is to be back in Cassie’s life. He will never make the same mistakes again. He will do whatever it takes to do what she needs him to do. He will do whatever it takes to <i>
  <u>Prove It.</u>
</i><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/d3f1db5a-ff42-4668-902f-6c30c933e6e2_zps57ca2209.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400340i/775614.jpg" alt=" photo d3f1db5a-ff42-4668-902f-6c30c933e6e2_zps57ca2209.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>It’s twisted how much she owns me. She always fucking has, but still.</b><br><br>It takes no time for Jack and Cassie to get back to being a couple. Being in the spotlight as ‘Jack Carter’s Girlfriend’ is much harder than Cassie would have thought. Between the ‘mean wives’, the media, the fans, and the evil ex-wife, it becomes too much for Cassie to take. But Cassie doesn’t want to worry Jack, she doesn’t want to let him in. When it finally gets to be too much for Cassie, and it feels like everyone is out to get them- will their love survive this- or will it crumble?<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/26851337-3b29-43ce-bf87-77b0368f9dcc_zps5c740cad.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400340i/775615._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 26851337-3b29-43ce-bf87-77b0368f9dcc_zps5c740cad.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>There is a little drama, but don’t worry readers- its nothing compared to the first book! Jack is amazing in this book. I fell for him all over again! I loved the back and forth between the past and present, and the fact that we got both Jack and Cassie’s pov. The epilogue was great. Now that Jack and Cassie’s story is over, would it be too much to ask for a Dean book ;) The Game Changer was a story of forgiveness, love, facing your fears and moving past your past. It gets 4.5 stars from me!<br><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%202/909ee271-ddbe-4333-8375-b6fb61da4999_zps7c6f9798.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400340i/775616.jpg" alt=" photo 909ee271-ddbe-4333-8375-b6fb61da4999_zps7c6f9798.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <blockquote>"You told me once that I was your game changer, but the thing is, you're mine too. It took me a while to realize that, but I finally did. You're my game changer. Because nothing else matters if you're not with me."</blockquote>
</b>  <br><br><br><i>*** I just realized I put the title of book one on my picture of this book... Maybe I need to quit writing reviews in the middle of the night with lack of sleep... sorry guys!***</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7402853859498917257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_513254128" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513254128" />
    <a title="lizparker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12782175-lizparker"><img alt="lizparker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372792093p2/12782175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513254128?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lizparker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lizparker" href="/user/show/12782175-lizparker">lizparker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12782175-lizparker?shelf=sports-jocks">sports-jocks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12782175-lizparker?shelf=contains-cheating">contains-cheating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12782175-lizparker?shelf=bad-boys">bad-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12782175-lizparker?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513254128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8890846896181945352">This book... this book.... ugh...this book typifies so much what is wrong with women today...this book makes me want to step on my soapbox with a big ass microphone... but I'll save that for the end. <br/><br/>Here's what you really want, to know<br/>Plot:<br/>The first 30% (kindle marked) of the book is all about Jack recapping how he spent that six months before he went to get Cassie back in New York, aka Kitten (what a dumb name btw). It's told in a writing style that kind of bothered me, but basically Jack and </span>
  <span id="freeText8890846896181945352" style="display:none">This book... this book.... ugh...this book typifies so much what is wrong with women today...this book makes me want to step on my soapbox with a big ass microphone... but I'll save that for the end. <br><br>Here's what you really want, to know<br>Plot:<br>The first 30% (kindle marked) of the book is all about Jack recapping how he spent that six months before he went to get Cassie back in New York, aka Kitten (what a dumb name btw). It's told in a writing style that kind of bothered me, but basically Jack and Cassie have just reunited and are making up for lost time between the sheets and in between sex and food, Jack is telling her what happened (mainly the drama surrounding him trying to separate from Chrystle, his ex-wife, aka the girl he cheated on Cassie with, the girl he left Cassie for, the girl who lied about being pregnant and the girl who refuses to give him an annulment)<br><br> <a href="http://gifsoup.com/view/4005661/you-crazy-bitch-whore.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380406179ra/792138.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://gifsoup.com" title="GIFSoup" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">GIFSoup</a><br><br>To be honest, I didn't like the writing style during that part- it was choppy going back and forth between C&amp;J now and J during those 6 months. But to each their own. Anywho, moving on. The rest of the book is about how basically Cassie is dealing with being the girlfriend of a professional athlete- only thing is people hate her because they think she is a home wrecker. She gets spit on, she has to deal with the other bitchy baseball spouses, crowds sneer at her basically her life is hell. But Cassie, being weak ass female, doesn't let Jack know what is going on (which how he can't know is beyond me... just seemed pretty unbelievable). When Jack finds out about how the media/fans are treating her he wanted to hire her some body guards, which she fights him on. Again- really Cassie?<br><br>Moving on, Cassie and Jack are not only struggling with the media but also with making time for one another due to their busy schedules. Enter in jealously and insecurities and you have a recipe for drama. Skip along to Cassie not being able to handle things, flying back to Cali to regroup with Melissa, a confrontation with ex-wife from hell Chyrstle, a Jack who wants to redeem himself, and you have a recipe for a happy ending, all tied in a nice little bow.<br><br><b>Things I Liked...</b><br>- Dean and Melissa- that is a "couple" I would enjoy reading more about for sure!!<br><br>- Matteo and Trina- more please!<br><br><b>Things I didn't like</b><br>- Cassie apologizes for every little thing. STOP FREAKIN APOLOGIZING. damn. She isn't the one who did anything wrong. She lets Jack get away with everything. When they talk about what happened during those 6 months, Cassie is appalled at how Chrystal acted calling her a bitch. Yeah- Chrystal was crazy, but YOUR BOYFRIEND is the one who decided to CHEAT ON YOU and bump uglies with crazy. Then he leaves you for her. HE IS TO BLAME. It was his decision to have sex with her- HIM. Don't lay the blame all on Crazy Chrystal's feet. <br><br>- I still don't feel like Jack redeemed himself. When you read his inner dialogue it's all about him. " I won't let her leave me... I can't live without her...I don't deserve you but I need you" He is essentially a selfish person. What about thinking what is best for Cassie? Jack runs the show. He decided when they broke up- he decided not to contact her FOR 6 MONTHS, he decided when they would get back together, he decides that Cassie will never leave him, because "he won't let her." It's all about Jack. What if he wasn't what was best for Cassie? (not that I like Cassie, obviously. She deserves what she gets because she is willing to take all of his shit). and THEN he has the audacity to think things like, <b>
  <i> "You can’t ever leave me for someone else.” The very fucking idea of Kitten leaving me for another guy made me want to rip someone’s head off. I’d die before I let that happen. This girl is my world."</i>
</b> Why the ever-lovin fuck does he think that he has the right to have thoughts like this after what he did. <br> <br><br><b>Now my soapbox. You have been warned...</b><br><br><b>
  <i> "Because being with him, no matter how illogical it seemed considering he was responsible for my internal carnage, completed me." </i>
</b>- weak ass, "I'm nothing without a man, and I would take him back no matter what he did/does to me"- aka Cassie<br><br>I want to apologize to J Sterling for using her book as my reference for my soapbox rant, (and believe me your book is the not the worst of the offenders) but I just don't understand the trend today among so many young adult romance authors to have these heroines who just eat shit from these guys with a smile. <br><br>These characters are weak protagonists- and set a horrible example for young women today. I'm a high school teacher, and everyday I see these young girls, who I know for a fact read the same books as I do, have some sort of unrealistic idea of how they should be treated in a relationship. I'm in my mid 20's, and these teenage girls/young women are coming up to me asking me questions about should they take their cheating boyfriends back. I mean WTF?! At this stage in their lives, their self worth is almost always on feeble ground and then they expect me to tell them how to react to a situation that is most definitely an "adult issue" situation. Can you imagine how crushed their fragile egos get when they witness their supposed boyfriends sexing it up with their supposed friends? And let me tell you- It happens ALL THE TIME! I think society is out of touch on what is going on with our young generation today and if you ask any teacher, they will tell you that we are creating and molding a generation of insecure, instant gratification, attention seeking individuals. <br><br>So where are the solutions? Unfortunately today, many of these young woman are growing up without strong male figures in their lives to teach them how they should be treated- so what do they do? They escape/resort to books to learn... and look at what they are learning. Three trends that I have noticed over and over is that <br>#1. I feel like they are learning that emotional abuse is ok <br>#2. That you need a man to complete who you are <br>#3. It's not love unless it's this all consuming, can't think, can't eat, need to be with them all hours of the day, can't live, I'll just die without them kind of love (which I would like to point out sound a little like obsession to me...but that's just me) <br><br>So here's what I would like to see a book capture<br>#1. Someone who inflicts "internal carnage" is not a keeper. Yes, you will get hurt in relationships, but you shouldn't get destroyed- if your world is "shattered" something is not right. Forgiveness is important, but you can forgive someone without taking them back when they have betrayed you. <br><br>#2. A woman must be WHOLE before she can fully give herself to her partner. If you think that you need man to be whole, then something is wrong. You, in and of yourself is enough. You should never need someone else to, "be enough." A man might make it easier, but another person shouldn't be necessary to make you who are are. (this is a generalization of course- I'm not saying that a spouse won't make you a better you, but the point is you are still YOU, with or without another person). <br><br>#3. I'm so sick of this OBSESSION portrayed as love. Most successful marriages are full of spouses who have separate, individual interests. You do not need to spend every waking minute of your life with your significant other to be in love. You don't have to "own them." Real love allows each person to be themselves, and nurtures their goals, both individually and as a couple. They make each other be the best person they can be- that doesn't mean they are just going to drop dead if something happened to their significant other. Believe it or not- people survive the loss of their spouses everyday and they are able to grieve and still enjoy their life. Life is easier with a partner- but it's not impossible without one.<br><br>Last one, and then I step off the soapbox.<br>For once, for the love of everything holy, can't we have a protagonist stand up for themselves and say, "You know what. I deserve better than this. I may have loved you, but I deserve someone who will NEVER cheat on me." (which you know, I think is pretty standard in most monogamous relationships). If women, as a whole, raised their standards for what they were looking for in a partner, then guess what- men as whole would rise up to meet them. True story-teachers are taught to have high expectations of their students, and every year we are amazed that not only did they meet those standards, but they exceeded them (a fact proven in both inner city and affluent schools, documented in many education journals). I fully believe that if women expected more from men, then men would not only meet those expectations, they would astonish us at what they are capable of doing. A girl can dream right?</span>
  <a data-text-id="8890846896181945352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

That I’m the one left standing all alone in a parking lot this time. I swear if my heart could leap out of my chest and into my hands, it would. I imagined that for a moment…the blood trickling through my fingertips, splashing onto the concrete below as I watched it slowly pound out its last beats before stopping altogether.<br />Fuck.<br />My life does not make sense without this girl. And now she’s gone.<br />Again.<br />How is it that I’m always losing her?<br /><br />Teaser #2:<br />I closed my eyes, drinking in his vow. Right now it lived on the outside of my skin, like an extra layer of warmth I couldn’t shed no matter how hot I became. My emotions had taken full control over every other part of me. I’d become victim to my own insecurities.<br />“I’ll show you,” his forehead pressed against mine as he continued. “I’ll never lose you again.”<br />“What if I want to be lost?” I teased with a serious tone and watched as he pulled his head from mine.<br />“I won’t let you.”<br />“You won’t let me?” I mocked, secretly loving the way he wanted me.<br />Jesus Cassie, you’re a fucking nutcase right now. Pick an emotion. Pretend like you’re in charge here.<br />“No. I won’t let you. End of discussion,” his mouth remained stoic.<br />“That wasn’t really what one would consider a discussion.”<br />“Because there’s nothing to discuss. I’m not leaving you ever again. And you’re not leaving me. No matter how pissed off I make you, or how frustrated. I fucking love you and I’m not going anywhere.”<br />I attempted to fight back the smile that formed. “And I love you. But really, if you ever cheat on me again I’ll cut your nuts off and hang them from the Empire State Building.” </i><br /><br /><br />Dear Ms. Sterling,<br />Am I reading the right teasers???!! Did Jack cheat AGAIN????!!!!!<br /><br /><br /><br />I am seriously pissed right now.Can't you just write something about DEAN? I THOUGHT Cassie and Fckin Jack Carter ALREADY HAVE THEIR H-E-A!!!!! HOW.COULD.YOU.DO.THIS????!!!! Please please don't make me unhappy, I love the first book too much drama but I still love it..But seriously????BK2??!! I can't stand cheating anymore and please tell me that bitch Chrystle is dead...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14158709654525934596"> <b>4 Happy and redeeming stars!!</b><br/><br/>so......<br/><br/><b>JACK FREAKING CARTER</b><br/><a href='http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/sexy%20smexy/jackcarter_zps5c45b0bb.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <span id="freeText14158709654525934596" style="display:none"> <b>4 Happy and redeeming stars!!</b><br><br>so......<br><br><b>JACK FREAKING CARTER</b><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/sexy%20smexy/jackcarter_zps5c45b0bb.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400408i/775830.jpg" alt=" photo jackcarter_zps5c45b0bb.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/sexy%20smexy/jack2_zps6f254f11.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400409i/775831.jpg" alt=" photo jack2_zps6f254f11.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>First of all if you haven't read book one go back and read about the angst and the rollercoaster that is Jack and Cassie and come back!<br>Ok for the rest of you I'll continue..<br><br>We start right from when we finished in the book one Jack and Cassie are together once again starting there new life in New York, but before Jack starts with his new team They both have a day to go over the past 6 months that they have been apart and why it took so long for Jack to get his act together, I have to say in this part of the story I loved going back in time and seeing it all from his perspective then back in present while they start fresh and sort old wounds out. <br><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/the%20game%20player/baseball-success_zps355cbe32.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400409i/775832._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo baseball-success_zps355cbe32.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/the%20game%20player/baseball_zpsb4ef44a7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400409i/775833._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo baseball_zpsb4ef44a7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But as they then start the path of recovery and again come together Cassie starts to struggle with being in the limelight as a girlfriend of a famous baseball player and with all the hurt and pain she's already been through can she stand strong and move forward together with Jack? is she strong enough to put her head high and ignore the press?!! <br><br><b>CASSIE</b><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/women%20pics/cassie_zpsdafdd548.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400409i/775834._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo cassie_zpsdafdd548.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Although I do love her being feisty and Independent and strong, I found Cassie to be a little irritating in this book. I just wanted her to not worry too much and just let Jack look after her, not that he didn't but Cassie fought it. <br><br>I think this story is very much love or hate you either hate them/him:<br><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/the%20game%20player/hatehim_zps92ece852.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400409i/775835.jpg" alt=" photo hatehim_zps92ece852.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Or you love them.. very much like Marmite right?!!<br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/the%20game%20player/marmite_zps7b1ac977.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400409i/775836.jpg" alt=" photo marmite_zps7b1ac977.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>For me I love Jack F'n Carter..<br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/the%20game%20player/love-him_zps681fa41f.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380400409ra/775837.gif" alt=" photo love-him_zps681fa41f.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Jack very much redeemed himself for me in this one, he proved his love to cassie time and time again and proved that he loved her implicitly. Above all they love each other and cannot live without the other in order to live, they're a perfect Mess. <br>Jack wants to protect his girl and keep her safe, life can be hard when your in the public eye though, but they learn in time to become a perfect team together. <br><br>The same characters that are in book one are again in here, Gran and Gramps oh how I wish I had grandparents like these they give out some pretty awesome advice..<br><blockquote>
  <b>"Love is life. If you miss out on love, You miss out on life."</b>
</blockquote><br><br>And Melissa is her hard assed self but adorable at the same time:<br><b>"Just remember one thing... when life gives you lemons, cut 'em open and squeeze the juice in life's face!!!"</b><br><br>Dean is pretty great as always there with Jack every step of the way. I just hope he gets his own HEA please write a story for him and Melissa please pretty please!<br><br>And again one NASTY BITCH!!! <br><br>So yes a journey on life and Love, If you enjoy New Adult go read I enjoyed and loved it but as I say MARMITE!! <br><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/nicole%20edwards%20books/temptationpic_zps7e9fdaab.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400409i/775838._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo temptationpic_zps7e9fdaab.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2456951430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer705802110107386960">4 ★'s <br/><br/>Okay, I wasn't particularly thrilled with the first book but there is just something about <i>Jack F*cking Carter</i> that made me <u>need</u> more. It didn't hurt that they would be older in this one and hopefully more mature. <br/><br/>The story picks right up where the last one ended...and it was very sweet. However, right after we get pushed back into all the emotional drama since Cassie has to know <i>everything</i> that happened. I'm a bit torn about some of the reasons but then I can understand some of the others</span>
  <span id="freeText705802110107386960" style="display:none">4 ★'s <br><br>Okay, I wasn't particularly thrilled with the first book but there is just something about <i>Jack F*cking Carter</i> that made me <u>need</u> more. It didn't hurt that they would be older in this one and hopefully more mature. <br><br>The story picks right up where the last one ended...and it was very sweet. However, right after we get pushed back into all the emotional drama since Cassie has to know <i>everything</i> that happened. I'm a bit torn about some of the reasons but then I can understand some of the others. <br><br>And can I just say that "Funsize" is pretty amazing? What a wonderful best friend! Her interactions with Chrystle had me cracking up!! <br><br>And the yummy parts with Funsize and you-know-her weren't too bad either!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397873326ra/9339944.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately, we then get thrust into the mean girl world and I really didn't care for it one bit. Surely, it can't be that bad?! <br><br>Some of the situations (again) were too cliché. I mean, the one with Matteo, come on! I can't imagine him <i>ever</i> doing that!<br><br>But what I can imagine is <u>exactly</u> what Chrystle did...sadly. Thank goodness for Vanessa...I was thoroughly shocked with that one. <br><br>The ending was really sweet and I was thrilled that two certain people finally got together...or did they?</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" href="/user/show/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts">Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer556361747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14678867889061315131">4 Perfect Sweet Jack Carter Stars<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412674i/811631._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/><i>The Game Changer</i> is about forgiveness, communication, trust, standing by your man, <b>
  <i>LOVE</i>
</b>, integrity, and one evil lying b*tch!!! <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ the painful subject of infidelity is explored <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>The additional characters add to the story and the troubles of our gorgeous couple, we see the bitch 'mean wives' club, a fabulously dishy driver and, of course, the lovely Dean & Melissa. (I'm hoping Dean gets his own story, he's a cutie. ♥) They all help t</span>
  <span id="freeText14678867889061315131" style="display:none">4 Perfect Sweet Jack Carter Stars<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412674i/811631._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><i>The Game Changer</i> is about forgiveness, communication, trust, standing by your man, <b>
  <i>LOVE</i>
</b>, integrity, and one evil lying b*tch!!! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the painful subject of infidelity is explored <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The additional characters add to the story and the troubles of our gorgeous couple, we see the bitch 'mean wives' club, a fabulously dishy driver and, of course, the lovely Dean &amp; Melissa. (I'm hoping Dean gets his own story, he's a cutie. ♥) They all help to move the story along with angst, drama, love and humour. <br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412674i/811632._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>♥"My life did not make sense without this girl."<br><br>♥"This girl is my world."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"..did you think she'd just leap into your arms and you'd live happily ever after?" ~ Dean </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This is what really bugged me in the first book; Jack's attitude and the fact that he never really questioned that Cassie would be available???<br><br>It's all about his emotions, how upset HE is? How things affect him? To a certain degree he is the same in this book but, he kind of has a realisation...it's like the penny drops. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You made the mistake, but she had to pay for it." ~ Melissa</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412674i/811634.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The Perfect Game left us with a HEA but, for me, it also left lots of unanswered questions and annoyances with character decisions and choices, like ~ Why did it take Jake 6 freaking months to go back to Cassie after <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ realising bitch face had lied about everything!!? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So, Jack has a story to tell, and we the reader <i>need</i> to hear it as much as Cassie, he needs redemption in our eyes.<br><br>His story of the missing time is just beautiful and gorgeous and made me completely fall in love with <i>Jack Sweet F'N Carter,</i> you warm to him...<br><br>♥He <i>
  <b>stalked</b>
</i> her...<br> <br>♥Always knew what she was doing....it made his absence acceptable...<br> <br>♥He <i>
  <b>cared</b>
</i> deeply <br><br>♥He was hurting, (we <u>desperately</u> needed to see that) <br><br>♥He needed to sort out <i>his</i> mistake first....<br><br>♥<b>Needed</b> to right his wrong.....be completely available...<br><br><br><i>
  <b>Could they overcome the past and have a future?</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412674i/811635.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He wrote letters to Cassie, letters he never sent. ♥ They were his therapy, they eased his conscience and inner turmoil. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I'm sorry for lying to you that morning. <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm sorry for cheating on you that night.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>I'm sorry for not being the person you knew I could be."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><i>And so you blinking SHOULD be!!! You were an arsehole!!! <br>♥ <b>Love</b> you now, though!!</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"....you two belong together."</b>
  </i>
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412674ra/811636.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>*****<br><br>Jack is now a major league Baseball player. An exceptionally talented pitcher, with notoriety and money. They experience the downside of fame and being in the public eye.....for Cassie, this is <b>NOT</b> a picnic.....its hell!!! <br><br>It affects her self-esteem. <br><br>*****<br><br><blockquote>
<b><i>"People spend their whole lives searching for the kind of love that the two of you share. That's what life is all about."</i></b><br><br><i>Will their love survive?</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412674i/811638.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i><b>♥"You're my Game Changer. Because nothing else matters if you're not with me."</b></i>~ Cassie<br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412674i/811639.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>This book is a <i>Game Changer</i> for me, it made me love the gorgeous <i> Sweet Jack f'n Carter</i> and the two book series a whole lot more. ♥ <br><br><br>♥ BR with the Gorgeous Pink Ladies, Barb &amp; Deanna ♥</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_650889714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/650889714" />
    <a title="Deanna❤Pink Lady❤️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14351108-deanna-pink-lady"><img alt="Deanna❤Pink Lady❤️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370640721p2/14351108.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/650889714?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna❤Pink Lady❤️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna❤Pink Lady❤️" href="/user/show/14351108-deanna-pink-lady">Deanna❤Pink Lady❤️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer650889714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15322865615313733712"><b>4 Curve Ball Stars</b><br/><br/>This story explains all the questions about the time Jack spent away from Cassie. It had been 6 months since Cassie had seen Jack when he showed up on her doorstep asking for another chance. We get to experience his viewpoint on his anguish, his hurt and his determination in getting back the love of his life after he made that one big f*cking mistake. <br/><br/><a href='http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/237d7b93-05e4-4ed2-aa93-b05b78542150_zpsd5f9c569.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426761i/852967.jpg' alt=' photo 237d7b93-05e4-4ed2-aa93-b05b78542150_zpsd5f9c569.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><a href='http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/94d45f9f-6ed3-47f5-89db-90aa6756ce90_zpsa9355578.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426761i/852968._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo 94d45f9f-6ed3-47f5-89db-90aa6756ce90_zpsa9355578.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Jack is truly a changed man. He gets himself traded to the NY Mets so that he can "Prove It" to Cassie that he can be th</span>
  <span id="freeText15322865615313733712" style="display:none"><b>4 Curve Ball Stars</b><br><br>This story explains all the questions about the time Jack spent away from Cassie. It had been 6 months since Cassie had seen Jack when he showed up on her doorstep asking for another chance. We get to experience his viewpoint on his anguish, his hurt and his determination in getting back the love of his life after he made that one big f*cking mistake. <br><br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/237d7b93-05e4-4ed2-aa93-b05b78542150_zpsd5f9c569.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426761i/852967.jpg" alt=" photo 237d7b93-05e4-4ed2-aa93-b05b78542150_zpsd5f9c569.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/94d45f9f-6ed3-47f5-89db-90aa6756ce90_zpsa9355578.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426761i/852968._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 94d45f9f-6ed3-47f5-89db-90aa6756ce90_zpsa9355578.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Jack is truly a changed man. He gets himself traded to the NY Mets so that he can "Prove It" to Cassie that he can be the man that she expected him to be and he will do whatever it takes to win her back. He is determined, loving, remorseful, apologetic, charming, and down right fuckingfantastic. He is after all <a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/image_zps9b073ecf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426761i/852969._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo image_zps9b073ecf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> Jack fucking Carter!!<br><br>Cassie must learn to trust Jack all over again,but her heart loves him, it just must get over the past to truly move on. Jack constantly apologies to Kitten. He promises that he won't mess up again. <br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/c57be20c-0ccd-4553-bead-5c2dec26e311_zpsa9cbb1b9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426761i/852970._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo c57be20c-0ccd-4553-bead-5c2dec26e311_zpsa9cbb1b9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>While he tells her his story, they take lots of breaks.<br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/Couples/tumblr_m9f4694q0S1rndbugo1_500_zps69cf4153.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408100ra/798078.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_m9f4694q0S1rndbugo1_500_zps69cf4153.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Even though they ease back into their relationship, there are still many obstacles thrown in their direction. Tabloids, paparazzi, ex-wife lies, mean baseball wives, and Cassie's own insecurities do a job at unraveling Jack and Cassie.<br><br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/0e788afb-bc3e-4318-bac8-29e7d50782a8_zps9161bb14.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426761i/852971._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 0e788afb-bc3e-4318-bac8-29e7d50782a8_zps9161bb14.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It takes a trip home for Cassie to open her eyes and really see and understand her relationship with Jack. Melissa, Dean, Gran and Gramps all help her with her unraveling. They have always been there for her, even when Jack wasn't. Gramp and Gran gives Cassie some advice-<br><br><b>What matters the most is who you love. Because when everything else is a distant memory, the people you love are all that's left. And love is the single most important thing we can do in our lives. Give it. Receive it. Teach others how to do it.<br><br>The older you get, the more you realize that it isn't about the material things, or pride or ego. It's about our hearts and who they beat for. I know your heart beats for Jack in the same way that his heart beats for you. I don't think one can survive without the other. Do you?<br><br>Love is life. If you miss out on love, you miss out on life.</b><br><br>With age comes wisdom and Gran and Gramp's advice is beautiful and real. There is a reason that they have been together all these years.<br><br>As you know at the end of The Perfect Game, Jack and Cassie set a date for their wedding. We get to read about the proposal and the wedding and also find out about couples who have gotten together and whose stories would make a great book!! But in getting to that point, Cassie and Jack grow as a couple, they love as a couple and most of all they learn to trust as a couple.<br><br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/f3a97c47-5f9a-41e9-b7a5-33c2ccd046af_zps0aec1321.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380426761i/852972.jpg" alt=" photo f3a97c47-5f9a-41e9-b7a5-33c2ccd046af_zps0aec1321.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I wasn't crazy with Cassie at times but can you really blame her for all her anxiety. She dealt with so much in book one that you weren't sure that she really could move past it. I know that Jack went above and beyond in proving and showing his Kitten that he was now that man she expected him to be. I fell in major love with Jack- yes me made a stupid mistake and he paid for it dearly, but he did "Prove It" to Cassie IMO. <br><br><a href="http://s1333.photobucket.com/user/Dpbarton/media/dbf33363a3ef9b7961fccbf21e3563bc_zps4916072f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380415091i/819196._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo dbf33363a3ef9b7961fccbf21e3563bc_zps4916072f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>BR with the extremely fabulous Pink Ladies ♥♥<br>I would definitely recommend both books!!<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15322865615313733712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13401775334024859761"><b>Final rating: 3.75</b><br/><br/><b>This review might contains little spoilers</b><br/><br/>The drama is <i>slightly</i> better than the first one. It's a continuation of what's left on the previous book when Jack Carter and Cassie Andrews reunited. 25%-30% of this book, we get to see Jack's point of view on <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15783307.The_Perfect_Game__The_Perfect_Game___1_' title='The Perfect Game (The Perfect Game, #1) by J. Sterling' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Perfect Game</a> during their breakup. It's nice hearing his side, despite of me being mad on his character.   <span id="freeText13401775334024859761" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 3.75</b><br /><br /><b>This review might contains little spoilers</b><br /><br />The drama is <i>slightly</i> better than the first one. It's a continuation of what's left on the previous book when Jack Carter and Cassie Andrews reunited. 25%-30% of this book, we get to see Jack's point of view on <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15783307.The_Perfect_Game__The_Perfect_Game___1_" title="The Perfect Game (The Perfect Game, #1) by J. Sterling" rel="nofollow noopener">The Perfect Game</a> during their breakup. It's nice hearing his side, despite of me being mad on his character. At least, he cleared up everything and he regrets it. <br /><br />The rest of the story is about Cassie Andrews difficulties on balancing her personal life and Jack's rising fame. She's not used to being on the spotlight as people tried to invade her private life by judging her because of the photo and articles that gave a wrong impression about her. These dramas affected her really bad. Sometimes it frustrates me she's not communicating well on Jack.<br /><br />I liked it. It's a happy ending, it's just that I can't help rolling my eyes on Cassie. Somehow, she frustrates me for being so over dramatic and weak. I don't buy that she "doesn't lead on" the driver. Girl, you're attracted with your hot driver. You may not love him but you still flirted with him. *more eye-rolling*</span>

<div id="review_532600228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/532600228" />
    <a title="Autumn Review" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6908049-autumn-review"><img alt="Autumn Review" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399327915p2/6908049.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/532600228?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Autumn Review" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Autumn Review" href="/user/show/6908049-autumn-review">Autumn Review</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6908049-autumn-review?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6908049-autumn-review?shelf=review">review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer532600228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16633118403497697460">I have to be honest, The Perfect Game stressed me out so much. It hit really close to home for me and I was troubled about it for days after. However, I did like Cassie and even though I wanted to smack Jack (more than once), his character is appealing. And I was happy with the ending, but going into THE GAME CHANGER, I really needed to see certain things happen. I really needed to see Jack redeem himself a bit more and I really needed a strong happy ending. That's a lot of really's, right? Well</span>
  <span id="freeText16633118403497697460" style="display:none">I have to be honest, The Perfect Game stressed me out so much. It hit really close to home for me and I was troubled about it for days after. However, I did like Cassie and even though I wanted to smack Jack (more than once), his character is appealing. And I was happy with the ending, but going into THE GAME CHANGER, I really needed to see certain things happen. I really needed to see Jack redeem himself a bit more and I really needed a strong happy ending. That's a lot of really's, right? Well, I'm pleased to say that I am firmly a Jack Carter fan now!<br /><br />Sterling sets the pace off strong by recapping what had happened during their time apart. I enjoyed that. I think it was important for Cassie to know that Jack was working hard to get back to her and to prove his love for her. As a result, I felt like I got into Jack's head more. I knew he loved Cassie in the first book, but in this book, I felt that he was truly devoted to her. <br /><br />There is some drama in this book, but nothing like the first book. At least in my opinion. Cassie struggles to find a balance between her life and the life she's created with Jack. Jack's celebrity is causing a lot of problems for her personally and she doesn't really know how to deal with it. Now I admit, that would be really hard to adjust to being criticized constantly and I probably would have reacted the same way about some of the things she dealt with. But instead of talking to Jack about it, she let it build and the result made my heart ache. Not necessarily for Cassie, but more for Jack. Jack puts so much effort into proving his love and earning her trust back and I felt that he deserved to know what she was going through. BUT, I had to remember that they are a young couple just starting out. Add in the pressure of celebrity and that's a tough combo. They had a lot to learn as a couple, but I was happy with how things ultimately came together. <br /><br />Ok, so I do love Jack now, but in the first book I really fell for his brother Dean. Well, in this book...I want to marry Dean. I absolutely love him and if I don't get a book for Dean, I might cry. He's just the sweetest and I'm dying to know more detail about his relationship with Melissa. I think they'd make a great story. <br /><br />Overall, I really liked it. I was happy with how the story played out. As I said, there is a different level of intensity to this one, but I thought it was fitting, as well as realistic. Fans of Cassie and Jack will be happy. If you're a fan of sports romance or even a fan of true love stories, check out this series!<br /><br />Quotes:<br /> ~Watching Jack play baseball was almost like having a spiritual awakening.-Loc 1558<br /><br />~"You told me once that I was your game changer, but the thing is, you're mine too. It took me a while to realize that, but I finally did. You're my game changer. Because nothing else matters if you're not with me."-Loc 3908</span>
  <a data-text-id="16633118403497697460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_475979712" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/475979712" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4087089-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368585032p2/4087089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/475979712?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/4087089-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer475979712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9236156113647256779">I have some mad love for J. Sterling. Not only as an author but as a genuinely nice person that cares about and talks with her fans. That being said, I find myself extremely lucky to have had the chance to read "The Game Changer" prior to its release. <br/><br/>This book for me was a solid 4 stars throughout most of it. I have this little requirement for a book to earn that 5th star...it has to evoke some sort of emotion in me, whether it be that it makes me cry, gives me goose bumps, turns me on, etc. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText9236156113647256779" style="display:none">I have some mad love for J. Sterling. Not only as an author but as a genuinely nice person that cares about and talks with her fans. That being said, I find myself extremely lucky to have had the chance to read "The Game Changer" prior to its release. <br /><br />This book for me was a solid 4 stars throughout most of it. I have this little requirement for a book to earn that 5th star...it has to evoke some sort of emotion in me, whether it be that it makes me cry, gives me goose bumps, turns me on, etc. The emotion has to reach out from the book and grab at my heart strings. Miss Sterling squeaked that out at the end for me and earned that 5th star.<br /><br />First off, if you haven't read "The Perfect Game" by J. Sterling, you need to go read that first. After reading it, if you felt pissed off at either Jack or Cassie so much that you wanted to throw your Kindle/Nook/paperback against the wall, then you need to read this book. Heck, you just need to read this even if you didn't get pissed off.<br /><br />The book starts off as flashbacks to different events that occurred in "The Perfect Game" giving you a look at what was going through Jack's mind as the story played out. Believe me, if you didn't love him before, your heart will reach out to him now. And don't worry; the story is not just a rewrite of "The Perfect Game" from Jack's perspective. Now that the drama from the past is behind them, they must learn (sometimes the hard way) how to handle life together with one of them being in the public eye and see if they have enough trust in each other to make it through as a couple.<br /><br />Aside from Jack and Cassie, many of the same characters from the first book make a second appearance in "The Game Changer" - Melissa and Dean in particular are a favorite of mine - with the addition of some other important (and HOT) characters. Miss Sterling has a way with creating characters that you either love to hate, hate to love, or simply can't help falling for.<br /><br />"The Game Changer" was a perfect continuation of the story started in "The Perfect Game." I was entertained, shocked, happy, sad, and utterly satisfied by the time I reached the end of the story. I would recommend this book to everyone that read "The Perfect Game" whether you loved it or hated it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9236156113647256779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_621750264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621750264" />
    <a title="Mika Pisueña" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16367499-mika-pisue-a"><img alt="Mika Pisueña" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368453310p2/16367499.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <span id="freeText17066093690295615057" style="display:none">Pre-reading:<br />What is this about?? I thought it ended with TPG? Seemed like a good ending for me at that time but what the hell, if Sterling wishes to write more of Jack and Cassie then I'm more than willing! Can't wait for the release! P.S. i kinda haven't completely forgiven Jack also.<br /><br />Post reading:<br />I stand by what I said pre-releasing of TGC, that TPG already had the perfect ending. I feel that the development of major conflicts were a bit lacking. Like Matteo's for example, his and Cassie's relationship were just on passing and suddenly he tells her that she loves her, kisses her and Jack is enraged? It would have been might more effective if Sterling focused on the growing relationship of the two as friends and the things that would have been factors to the accusation of cheating. Anyway, thank you Sterling for giving us a glimpse of Jack and Cassie's life after TPG.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SFRC1OV8q4wpoC5mtN0LLsxbB7K9fnoF19A6Ln030aZwdvDqlGWfX/1gKjpM5w5JptBmc1J5gxcqTX7JrF5yaA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zhb59j0oLpu5ZEFePoojj76i2YJbB83jEVChYV18Kfv2NEvITDEaSG2kRQLGsCbo1Cm4Q7QANPHszeWGjBWKNQ==')})
  }

The son of a hometown football legend and the brother of a local football hero, Reed wore all the pressures of carrying a town without hope into the spotlight. Thankfully, he had the talent to back it up. But when he meets a girl who makes him think twice about exactly what being a hero means, he starts to wonder if following in his brother’s footsteps might be all wrong. \n\nNolan Lennox was everything that was opposite of expected. She didn’t flirt, she didn’t drink and she didn’t sleep around. Nothing about her was easy, but something about her made Reed want to try harder. Though she didn’t look the part, she seemed to be spending a lot of time in Reed’s thoughts, and he wondered if she could be the one who made it all worthwhile. But could Reed handle letting her down? And would breaking her heart break him beyond repair?\n\nWaiting on the Sidelines explores young love to its fullest, exposing how real young heartbreak and passion is and how important it is to discover yourself and hold onto your own identity. The story follows two young characters as they deal with mature situations, including the prevalence of bullying and promiscuity in today’s high school setting.
